## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetic rate laws expressed as ODEs. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are empirical or mechanistic rate laws where the instantaneous rate depends on A and possibly explicitly on time via changing conditions or deactivation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of concentration; surface-limited or saturated catalyst regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction with other reactant approximately proportional to A)
- nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (approach to steady state A_eq = c0/(c1); chemostat/feed-removal balance)
- Reversible first-order to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating then limiting (quadratic): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed growth with depletion/limitation at A≈c1)
- Time-dependent first-order (exponential deactivation of rate constant): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective k(t) decreases due to catalyst decay or inhibition buildup)
- Time-dependent first-order (warming/aging ramp proxy): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective k(t) increases with time under changing conditions)
- Periodic forcing of rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated kinetics, e.g., light-driven or oscillatory conditions)
- Saturating-in-A consumption (capacity-limited): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate increases with A then approaches -c0 at high A; transport/catalyst-site limitation)
- Inhibition-like saturation: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A**c2) (high-A inhibition or crowding reduces effective rate at large A)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over wide A, a zero-order term (-c0) is indicated (flat rate vs A).
- If dA_dt versus A is a straight line through the origin (negative slope), first-order kinetics (-c0*A) is suggested.
- If plotting -dA_dt versus A on log-log axes gives a line, the slope estimates the reaction order in -c0*A**c1.
- A nonzero intercept in dA_dt vs A (crossing dA_dt=0 at A=c0/c1) indicates approach to a steady state (c0 - c1*A) or equilibrium (-c0*(A-c1)).
- If the magnitude of dA_dt initially grows in time at fixed A, include explicit time-dependence in the rate coefficient (e.g., exp(c*t) or sin(c*t) modulation).
- If |dA_dt| increases with A at low A but levels off at high A, use a saturating form in A such as -c0*A/(A+c1).
- If the rate is maximal at intermediate A and small near A≈0 and A≈c1, a quadratic autocatalytic/limiting structure c0*A*(c1-A) is plausible.
- If the system slows down over time even at similar A, model catalyst deactivation/aging via a decaying prefactor exp(-c*t) multiplying an A-dependent rate.
- If high concentrations appear to suppress the rate (crowding/product inhibition proxy), use denominators that grow faster than A (e.g., A/(c1 + A**c2)).

### 27
Everything over \(c1+\text{Abs}(A)^4\). On domain \(A\ge 0\), denominator \(c1+A^4\) looks promising (can match \(1+kA^4\) up to scaling). But numerator terms are of forms:
- \(A\cdot A^4 = A^5\) term,
- \(A\) terms,
- \(\text{Abs}(A)^{c5}\) terms,
- log terms.
To match GT, we must eliminate log terms: set \(c6=0,c9=0\). Also eliminate unwanted powers: set \(c0=0,c2=0,c3=0,c4=0,c8=0\) unless \(c5\) chosen to create \(A^2\). But numerator pieces available for pure power are \(\text{Abs}(A)^{c5}\) and \(\text{Abs}(A)^{4+c5}\). To get \(A^2\) you’d need \(c5=2\), giving numerator terms \(A^2\) and \(A^6\). You can set the \(A^6\) coefficient (via \(c8\)) to 0, leaving \(\propto A^2/(c1+A^4)\). That matches the *shape* of the rational term, but GT is
\[
- \alpha A^2 + \beta \frac{A^2}{1+kA^4},
\]
i.e. **polynomial plus rational**. Candidate 27 is **only** a single rational expression with denominator \(c1+A^4\); it cannot produce an additional standalone \(-\alpha A^2\) term unless the numerator contains an \(-\alpha A^2(c1+A^4)\) part, which would require an \(A^6\) term tied to the same coefficient pattern. But with \(c5=2\), you could keep an \(A^6\) term to generate \(-\alpha A^2\) after division? Check:
\[
\frac{pA^6 + qA^2}{c1+A^4} = pA^2 + \frac{q - pc1}{c1+A^4}A^2.
\]
This indeed yields a polynomial \(pA^2\) plus a rational \(A^2/(c1+A^4)\) term. Great. So candidate 27 **can** represent \(A^2\) polynomial + \(A^2/(c1+A^4)\) rational, on domain \(A\ge 0\).
We can set:
- domain condition: \(A\ge 0\) so Abs drops.
- set \(c5=2\).
- set log terms off: \(c6=0, c9=0\).
- set linear-in-\(A\) terms off: \(c0=0,c2=0,c3=0\).
Then candidate reduces to
\[
\frac{c4 A^2 + c8 A^6}{c1 + A^4}.
\]
Rewrite:
\[
= c8 A^2 + \frac{(c4 - c8 c1)A^2}{c1 + A^4}.
\]
Match GT by choosing:
- \(c8 = -0.18997742423620262\).
- Need denominator \(c1 + A^4\) to equal \(1 + 0.7497988950401423 A^4\) up to scaling. But here coefficient of \(A^4\) is 1, constant is \(c1\). We can scale:
\[
\frac{A^2}{1+kA^4} = \frac{1}{k}\frac{A^2}{A^4 + 1/k}.
\]
So set \(c1 = 1/k = 1/0.7497988950401423\).
Then require
\[
\frac{(c4 - c8 c1)A^2}{c1 + A^4} = \beta \frac{A^2}{1+kA^4}
= \frac{\beta}{k}\frac{A^2}{A^4 + 1/k}
\]
With \(c1=1/k\), this becomes \((c4 - c8 c1)=\beta/k\).
So set \(c4 = c8 c1 + \beta/k\), where \(\beta=0.45987487478174419\).
All constants are free, so feasible. Therefore **candidate 27 matches GT on domain \(A\ge 0\)** (and also \(A\le 0\) would work similarly because even powers only; but we used Abs anyway).

So 27 is a **match**.

**GT:** `-0.18997742423620262*A**2 + 0.45987487478174419*A**2/(0.7497988950401423*A**4 + 1)`

Let me simplify the GT. The GT has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `-A²`
2. A rational term `A²/(c₄*A⁴ + 1)`

So GT = `α*A² + β*A²/(γ*A⁴ + 1)` where α ≈ -0.19, β ≈ 0.46, γ ≈ 0.75.

This can be written as a single fraction: `[α*A²*(γ*A⁴ + 1) + β*A²] / (γ*A⁴ + 1)` = `[α*γ*A⁶ + (α+β)*A²] / (γ*A⁴ + 1)`

The key structural features:
- It's a function of A only (not t)
- It's a rational function: polynomial in A divided by (γ*A⁴ + 1)
- Numerator has A⁶ and A² terms
- No transcendental functions (no sin, log, exp)

Let me check candidates systematically:

**Candidates with sin, log, exp, or other transcendental functions** cannot match unless those terms can be zeroed out. Let me check which ones can have transcendental terms zeroed:

For candidates with `sin(...)`, `log(...)`, `exp(...)` terms - I can set their coefficients to 0 if they're additive. But then the remaining terms must match the GT structure.

**Candidate 10:** `[A⁷c₀ + A⁶c₂ + A⁵c₃ + A²c₄ + Ac₅ + Ac₆ + c₇] / (A⁵ + c₁)`

GT as single fraction: `[α*γ*A⁶ + (α+β)*A²] / (γ*A⁴ + 1)`

Candidate 10 denominator is A⁵ + c₁, GT denominator is γ*A⁴ + 1. These have different degrees, so they can't match. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 11:** Same denominator A⁵ + c₁. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 20:** `A*c₀ + A*c₁/(A^c₂ + c₃) + A*c₄/(A*c₅ + c₆) + c₇/(A*c₅ + c₆)`

Setting c₀=0, this has terms with denominators (A^c₂ + c₃) and (A*c₅ + c₆). GT has denominator (γA⁴+1). If c₂=4, then A*c₁/(A⁴+c₃) gives A/(A⁴+c₃), but GT needs A²/(A⁴+1). Can't get A² in numerator from A*c₁. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `A*c₀ + A^c₁*c₂/(A^c₁ + c₃) + c₄*log(c₅*exp(A*c₆) + 1)`

Set c₄=0 to kill log. Then: `A*c₀ + c₂*A^c₁/(A^c₁ + c₃)`. Set c₁=2: `c₀*A + c₂*A²/(A² + c₃)`. GT needs A²/(A⁴+1) type term. A²/(A²+c₃) ≠ A²/(A⁴+1). Set c₁=4: c₂*A⁴/(A⁴+c₃) which is not A²/(A⁴+c₃). [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 36:** `[A⁵c₀ + A⁴c₂*sin(...) + Ac₅ + Ac₆ + c₇*sin(...)] / (A⁴ + c₁)`

Set sin coefficients to 0: `[A⁵c₀ + A(c₅+c₆)] / (A⁴+c₁)`. GT numerator needs A⁶ and A² terms. This has A⁵ and A. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 40:** `[A⁵c₀ + A⁴c₂*log(...) + A(c₄+c₅) + c₆*log(...)] / (A⁴+c₁)`

Set log coefficients to 0: `[A⁵c₀ + A(c₄+c₅)] / (A⁴+c₁)`. Same issue. [NO MATCH]
